# SkillForge Backlog

> Single source of truth for all work items: bugs, enhancements, and tech debt.
> Spec files in `docs/specs/` describe the *what* and *how*. This file tracks the *what's-next* and *what's-done*.

## Rules
- **IDs are immutable.** Once assigned, a B-### or E-### never changes, never gets reused.
- **One row per item.** Don't split, don't merge. Spawn a new ID if scope splinters.
- **Status is the only field Claude Code may flip autonomously** (🔴 → 🟡 → ✅). All other fields require human edit.
- **Closing an item:** status → ✅ + append a one-liner to Notes: `closed by <commit-sha> on <YYYY-MM-DD>`.
- **Priority is a product decision.** Set by Dhamo only.
- **Spec column is the on-disk path** (`docs/specs/phase-N/NN-name.md`). Empty if no spec exists yet — create one before implementation.

## Status legend
- 🔴 Pending (not started)
- 🟡 In progress / partial / blocked
- ✅ Done
- ⚪ Won't do / deferred indefinitely
- 🟦 Back-burner — scoped out, awaiting activation gate (e.g., telemetry threshold). Not worked on until the gate trips.

## Priority legend
- **P0** — broken in production, blocking users, blocking next milestone
- **P1** — committed for this phase
- **P2** — wanted, not committed
- **P3** — someday / nice-to-have

---

| B-014 | ats-scanner | Section rewrite path missing `thinking_budget` → Gemini 2.5 Pro MAX_TOKENS → 502 "Regenerate with Resume" | P0 | ✅ | docs/specs/phase-5/51-ai-rewrite-section-preservation.md | (from 2026-04-21 E2E bug diagnosis) | Closed 2026-04-21 by `067c232`. Regression inside spec #51's own B-001 fix — pure bug fix, R14 exception (b). Root cause: `gpt_service.py:380-387` (chunked `_rewrite_one_section`) and `:615-622` (per-section endpoint `generate_section_rewrite`) called `generate_for_task(task="resume_rewrite_section", max_tokens=SECTION_MAX_TOKENS=2500, ...)` without `thinking_budget`, so Gemini 2.5 Pro's reasoning tier consumed ~2497 tokens on internal thinking, hit `FinishReason.MAX_TOKENS`, and returned empty text → `RewriteError("rewrite_parse_error")` → HTTP 502. The full-rewrite fallback at `:487-495` already passed `thinking_budget=FULL_REWRITE_THINKING_BUDGET` correctly — the section path was the only omission. Fix: added `SECTION_THINKING_BUDGET = 800` constant, bumped `SECTION_MAX_TOKENS = 2500 → 4000` for headroom, passed `thinking_budget=SECTION_THINKING_BUDGET` to both section call sites. Regression tests in `tests/services/test_resume_rewrite.py` (+3): guard section-call signature contains `thinking_budget`, guard per-section endpoint same, guard constant-level headroom invariant (`SECTION_MAX_TOKENS >= 2 * SECTION_THINKING_BUDGET`). Diagnosis: `docs/status/E2E-BUG-DIAGNOSIS-2026-04-21.md` §Bug (a) + `backend.log:149-178` (thoughts_token_count=2497, max_tokens=2500). |
| B-015 | frontend | axios response interceptor swallows daily-wall 402 payload ("[object Object]" toast, no PaywallModal) | P1 | ✅ | | (from 2026-04-21 E2E bug diagnosis) | Closed 2026-04-21 by `edf908b`. Regression surface inside shipped specs #50 + #42 — pure bug fix, R14 exception (b). Root cause: `api.ts` response interceptor unconditionally toasted `error.response.data.detail` for non-401 errors; for the 402 daily-review wall the detail is an object, so users saw "[object Object]" / "An unexpected error occurred" instead of `QuizPanel` rendering `PaywallModal` / `WallInlineNudge`. Fix: (1) wall-aware pass-through — 402 responses whose `detail.trigger` is a string are component-owned UX and skip the toast; (2) object-coercion guard — only string `error`/`detail` values are toasted, anything else falls through to `error.message` / "An unexpected error occurred". Regression tests in `tests/services/api.interceptor.test.ts` (+8 FE, 182→190). Diagnosis: `docs/status/E2E-BUG-DIAGNOSIS-2026-04-21.md` §Bug (b). |

| B-021 | interview | Cover letter prompt always receives "your company" — `extract_job_requirements` never populates `company_name` | P2 | ✅ | | (from 2026-04-22 bug report — surfaced as "Conversational tone regen doesn't pull JD company details") | Closed 2026-04-22 by `e7c6d73`. Shipped: `nlp.py` gains heuristic `_extract_company_name(jd_text) -> str | None` using 5 high-precision regex patterns (`About X:` / `About X —`, `Join [the] X team/as/in`, `X is hiring/looking for/seeking`, `at X.` position anchor, `Company: X` line). `extract_job_requirements` now returns `"company_name": str | None` in its dict — two live consumers pick it up automatically: `gpt_service.generate_cover_letter` prompt reads it instead of defaulting to "your company", and `api/routes/analyze.py` tracker autopopulate writes real company names instead of "Unknown Company". Low-confidence JDs return None, and both consumer fallbacks ("your company" / "Unknown Company") remain intact for that case — silent misses are strictly better than false positives ending up in the prompt. `_COMPANY_TOKEN` uses `[ \t]+` (not `\s+`) between Title-Case words to prevent the regex backtracking across blank lines and absorbing a preceding headline. Tone-agnostic root cause; three-tone parametrized test guards tone invariance. Tests: BE +19 (9 happy-path parametrized extractor cases, 4 None-fallback cases, 3 tone × company-flows-into-prompt, 1 fallback-preserved, 1 shape-stability, 1 populated end-to-end). No new endpoint, no schema change, no LLM call. **Deliberately NOT in scope:** FE `CoverLetterRequest.company_name` override field (user-confirmed company name), LLM-based extraction, batch-backfill of existing "Unknown Company" tracker rows. | `hirelens-backend/app/services/nlp.py::extract_job_requirements` returns `required_skills, preferred_skills, all_skills, job_title, seniority_level, responsibilities` — no `company_name`. Three consumers read `jd_requirements.get("company_name")` and all fall through to placeholder: `gpt_service.py:658` → `"your company"` (cover-letter prompt, the bug surface), `api/routes/analyze.py:209` → `"Unknown Company"` (tracker autopopulate rows), `ai_service.py:148` (dead code — S47-defer, spec #52 §2). **Tone-agnostic**: bug surfaces most on Conversational because formal tones mask "your company" with ceremonial language; Conversational expects personable specificity. **Fix shape:** add a heuristic `_extract_company_name(jd_text)` to `nlp.py` (consistent with `_detect_seniority` / `_extract_responsibilities` regex approach); `extract_job_requirements` includes `"company_name": <str | None>` in its return dict. Fallback "your company" / "Unknown Company" strings in consumers remain for the low-confidence case — benign when extraction misses. Two live consumers improve simultaneously. No new endpoint, no schema change, no new LLM call. Tests: `nlp.py` unit tests for the extractor across common JD shapes; cover-letter service test that end-to-end the prompt receives the extracted name instead of "your company" when the JD contains a known-pattern company mention. |
| B-020 | home | TodaysReviewWidget should surface free-tier daily-wall-hit state | P3 | 🔴 | docs/specs/phase-5/50-free-tier-daily-card-wall.md | (follow-up to B-019 2026-04-22) | Free-tier users are capped at 10 card reviews per user-local-midnight day (spec #50 / E-030; LD-001 amendment 2026-04-26 lowered the cap from 15 → 10). | B-026 | design-system | Native `<input type="date">` calendar icon invisible on dark themes — `color-scheme` never set on `:root` | P2 | ✅ | | (from 2026-04-22 bug report — PersonaPicker date field on "What brings you to SkillForge?" page) | Closed 2026-04-22 by `a436364`. Root cause: the app has 3 themes applied via CSS variables (`applyTheme` in `src/styles/design-tokens.ts:319-325`) but never sets the browser's `color-scheme` property on the theme-target element. Browsers render native `<input type="date">` calendar icons + scrollbars + number spinners using the effective `color-scheme` (defaults to `light`), so on Dark and Midnight Blue themes the calendar icon is dark-grey on dark background — effectively invisible. Not scoped to PersonaPicker; the issue affects every native form control app-wide. **Fix shape (design-system-level, zero per-component edits):** extended the `Theme` interface with `colorScheme: 'dark' | 'light'`; declared it per-theme (`dark: 'dark'`, `midnight-blue: 'dark'`, `light: 'light'`); made `applyTheme` also set `el.style.colorScheme = theme.colorScheme`. Every native picker/scrollbar/spinner now renders in sympathy with the active theme, including after runtime theme switches. No CSS-file edits, no Tailwind config change, no `color-scheme` utility sprinkled through components. **Not a retrofit or new feature — R14 exception (b) pure bug fix.** Tests: FE 214 unchanged (visual behavior of native browser chrome isn't unit-test surface; `tsc --noEmit` clean confirms the interface extension). **Deliberately NOT in scope:** broader cross-browser date-picker redesign (deferred — native picker is the established UX per spec #53 LD-2), custom-theming of `::-webkit-calendar-picker-indicator` beyond what `color-scheme` provides, `meta[name="color-scheme"]` setting for initial-paint behavior (would be a micro-optimization). |

| B-024 | interview | Cover letter and tracker autopopulate render "your company" / "Unknown Company" for valid JDs — `_extract_company_name` regex recall gap | P1 | ✅ | | (from 2026-04-22 bug report with artifact — JPMorgan JD) | Closed 2026-04-22 by `50e3c3c`. Root cause: B-021's `_extract_company_name` used 5 high-precision regex patterns with intentionally narrow recall (precision-first). Real JDs in shapes not covered by the patterns — including the JPMorgan Chase & Co. JD used in the bug repro, which uses a standalone-header-line shape (`"JPMorgan Chase & Co.\n"`) with no `About X:` / `Join X` / `X is hiring` anchor — returned None and the cover-letter prompt fell through to `"your company"`, tracker autopopulate to `"Unknown Company"`. Verified against the JPMorgan JD: 0 of 5 patterns matched. **Three-layer design shipped (layers 1 + 3):** (1) LLM primary — new `company_name_extraction` task on FAST tier (`gemini-2.0-flash` default) in `llm_router.py`; prompt explicitly instructs null-on-unclear, rejects role-title / aggregator responses, preserves verbatim capitalization. (2) Manual user entry on null — **deferred to B-025** (separate spec required). (3) Existing `"your company"` / `"Unknown Company"` consumer fallback preserved for the null case. **Orchestrator policy** (`nlp.py::_extract_company_name`): LLM raises (network/quota/config) → regex fallback (preserves pre-B-024 behavior on transient outages); LLM returns null (valid "unclear" judgment) → return None (do NOT re-try regex — null is data, not error); LLM returns string → aggregator deny-list backstop (`{linkedin, indeed, glassdoor, monster, ziprecruiter, careerbuilder, dice, wellfound, angellist, simplyhired}`), 100-char length cap, return. **Role-title rejection** enforced in the LLM prompt (not server-side) per the "STOP if validator gets more complex than deny-list" guard — cleaner boundary and avoids collision with `extract_job_requirements`'s buggy first-line `job_title` heuristic. Both live consumers inherit the fix transparently (cover-letter prompt + `api/routes/analyze.py` tracker autopopulate). **Cost impact:** adds one Flash call (~1k input + ~50 output tokens ≈ $0.00014) per `extract_job_requirements` invocation, which fires once per ATS scan and once per cover-letter generation. Negligible at current scale (~$1.40/mo per 10k scans). **Latency impact:** +500-800ms per scan (Flash median) — acceptable trade-off under precision-first policy. Tests: BE +10 (`test_nlp.py`): positive (JPMorgan JD, LLM mocked to return verbatim); null → None without regex fallback; aggregator rejection (case-sensitive + case-insensitive); empty-string output → None; malformed JSON → None (treated as null, not infra failure); infra-failure → regex-fallback happy; infra-failure + regex-miss → None; empty-JD short-circuit before LLM call; 100-char length cap. Existing B-021 9-positive + 4-negative parametrized tests renamed to target `_extract_company_name_regex` directly so fallback path stays covered independently. End-to-end `extract_job_requirements` tests now mock the LLM explicitly. **Deliberately NOT in scope:** B-025 layer 2 (manual entry UI), LLM prompt tuning for better recall, role-title server-side rejection (prompt-enforced), tracker backfill of existing "Unknown Company" rows. **D-016 stays 🟡 open** — unrelated latent gap (cover-letter `response_schema` never plumbed). |
| B-023 | interview | Cover letter signature renders "KEY ACHIEVEMENTS" (or other all-caps section header) — `_extract_candidate_name` false-positive matches all-caps resume headers | P1 | ✅ | | (from 2026-04-22 bug report with artifact) | Closed 2026-04-22 by `79f76b4`. Root cause: `gpt_service.py::_extract_candidate_name` walked the first 10 resume lines and accepted any 2–4-token line where every token matched `^[A-Z][A-Za-z.'-]+$` — that regex silently accepts all-uppercase tokens (`"KEY"`, `"ACHIEVEMENTS"`) because `[A-Za-z]+` allows uppercase. When the candidate's real name was not in the first 10 lines, the helper returned a section header instead. The header was then interpolated into the cover-letter prompt as the signature field, the LLM dutifully echoed it, and `_join_cover_letter` rendered "Sincerely,\nKEY ACHIEVEMENTS" unchanged. **NOT a schema-enforcement issue** — the LLM output was structurally valid JSON; the prompt was feeding it a poisoned candidate_name. D-016 (missing `response_schema`) stays 🟡 open as a separate latent defense-in-depth gap; neither B-023 nor B-024 closes it. **Fix shape:** self-documenting early-return guard — before the token-regex check, skip any line that is pure-uppercase (`line == line.upper()` after confirming at least one letter is present, so digit/punct-only lines fall through to the existing guards). Human names capitalize the first letter per token, not every letter — no legitimate candidate-name line is pure-uppercase. Tests: BE +12 (`test_cover_letter_format.py`): 6 parametrized positives (`"Jordan Doe"`, `"Dhamo Sankaran"`, `"Mary-Kate O'Neill"`, `"Alice Johnson"`, `"Dr. Alice Johnson"`, `"Jean-Luc Picard"`) + 4 parametrized all-caps negatives (`"KEY ACHIEVEMENTS"`, `"PROFESSIONAL SUMMARY"`, `"WORK EXPERIENCE"`, `"EDUCATION"`) + 1 skips-header-finds-real-name-below + 1 blank-resume fallback. **Deliberately NOT in scope:** B-024 (separate row, on hold for JD text) — company-name regex recall gap that produces the "your company" leak surfaced in the same artifact. Root causes do not overlap; schema enforcement would not close either. |

| B-036 | telemetry | `scan_rehydrated` PostHog event missing `scan_age_days` property — deferred from P5-S59-impl judgment call #2 | P3 | 🟦 | docs/specs/phase-5/59-scan-persistence.md (§12 / §17) | (deferred from spec #59 / `0b35440`) | Spec §12 specified `scan_age_days: integer \| null` on the `scan_rehydrated` event; impl deferred per the §17 open question — `AnalysisResponse` does not carry `scan_created_at` and the FE has no other source for the tracker row creation timestamp. | B-114 | billing | Webhook handler `.get()` → bracket-access fix (Stripe SDK v14+ StripeObject API change) — closes E-033 + E-039 | P0 | ✅ | docs/audits/stripe-integration-audit-2026-05.md (live-triage finding) | `<this-slice>` (filed + closed in same slice) | Closed `<this-slice>` 2026-05-02. **P0 production hotfix.** Live triage on Dhamo's test-mode upgrade flow surfaced that EVERY webhook (5 distinct events) returned 500 with `AttributeError: get` at `payment_service.py:251` (`event.get("id", "")`). Root cause: Stripe SDK v14+ stopped subclassing `dict` for `StripeObject`; `.get()` no longer exists, only bracket + attribute access. Tests passed because every fixture mocked `construct_event` with a plain `dict` — test/prod parity gap. **Fix:** new `_field(obj, key, default)` helper at `payment_service.py:60-72` (isinstance-dispatched: `dict.get` for test fakes, `getattr` for StripeObject). Bracket access `event["id"]` replaces `event.get("id", "")` (Stripe Events always carry an id). All 5 `.get()` callsites in `_handle_checkout_completed` + `_handle_subscription_deleted` + analytics_track payload migrated to `_field()`. **Test parity fix:** 2 new regression tests (`test_webhook_handles_real_stripe_event_object` + `test_webhook_handles_unhandled_event_type_with_real_object`) use `stripe.Event.construct_from()` instead of plain dicts → catches the next SDK rename automatically. 4 prior `fake_event` dicts updated to include `id` field (test parity hygiene; matches reality). **Tests:** BE 834 → 836 (+2 in envelope) under prod-default env; FE 466 unchanged. Live verification: signed-payload repro pre-fix raised `AttributeError: get`, post-fix returns `{'received': True, 'event_type': 'invoice.finalized'}`. **JC #1 (info-only):** Step-1 fix to `event["id"]` exposed the same `.get()` pattern in `_handle_*` dispatchers — surfaced via the new regression test (working as designed). Validates SHA via `git rev-parse --verify`, enumerates files containing the marker via `grep -rl --include='*.md'` across the canonical scope (BACKLOG.md + SESSION-STATE.md + docs/specs/), and substitutes via portable `sed | mv` temp-file pattern (avoids `sed -i` BSD-vs-GNU split). `--dry-run` prints per-file line numbers + proposed substitutions without writing. | E-046 | tracker | Real-time recruiter-call AI copilot | P3 | 🟦 | | (from 2026-04-23 product-scope conversation) | **DO-NOT-BUILD (permanent rejection).** Explicit rejection row exists so future sessions do not re-litigate this scope. **Rationale:** (a) TOS-violation surface on target employers' interview processes (recording / AI-listening on a recruiter call without explicit consent violates most major employers' interview conduct policies and some states' one-party-recording-law liability frameworks); (b) one-party-recording-law liability varies by jurisdiction (California / Illinois / Maryland + several others require two-party consent — a nationwide product cannot quietly assume one-party); (c) commoditized LLM-wrapper space — no moat extension from current study-loop differentiation; (d) support burden for the 5% of users who'd use it outweighs revenue upside at our scale. **No gate.
